  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_496e77d8-0f9d-440e-adb5-7f511275f220'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer2439162452967391974">An ancient curse robbed Gemma Fisher of everything that matters most—her friends, her family and the guy she loves.   <span id="freeText2439162452967391974" style="display:none">An ancient curse robbed Gemma Fisher of everything that matters most—her friends, her family and the guy she loves. But now that she found the scroll that binds the curse, she finally has a chance to get her old life back. She just needs to destroy the scroll—but it's not as easy as she hoped. Protected by ancient magic, it seems utterly indestructible. Making matters worse, Penn has grown even more obsessed with stealing Daniel for her own…and she's about to succeed.<br /><br />Gemma's frantic search leads her to someone who might be able to help—the mysterious immortal who cursed Penn and her sisters thousands of years ago. As Gemma and her friends unravel the tragic history of the curse, they plunge deeper into a world of shocking secrets and twisted vendettas—and it'll take all their courage, love and the power of their friendship just to survive. Gemma has so much to fight for and she's never wanted anything more, but will it be enough to stop her enemies?</span>

Although it was the best book in the series, you have to start with book one and work your way up to this book. But, the rest of the series is totally worth reading, I loved this series!!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696217490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1425654297401350486">Actual rating: 1.5 <b>Rounded up to 2 because THIS BOOK MEANS THE SERIES IS OVER</b>.<br/><br/>I have this beautiful nail polish with an interesting texture. It looks really cool, but wearing it is a different story. I have contact lenses, you see, and while an awesome sandy texture may LOOK good, if you've ever had sand in your eyes, you know it's fucking painful. Such is my experience every time I remove my contacts, it's like sand rubbing against my eyeballs, and yet I keep on using that damn polish anyway, a</span>
  <span id="freeText1425654297401350486" style="display:none">Actual rating: 1.5 <b>Rounded up to 2 because THIS BOOK MEANS THE SERIES IS OVER</b>.<br><br>I have this beautiful nail polish with an interesting texture. It looks really cool, but wearing it is a different story. I have contact lenses, you see, and while an awesome sandy texture may LOOK good, if you've ever had sand in your eyes, you know it's fucking painful. Such is my experience every time I remove my contacts, it's like sand rubbing against my eyeballs, and yet I keep on using that damn polish anyway, and will probably finish the bottle at the expense of scarring my corneas.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380433254i/871754.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Such has been my experience with the <i>Watersong</i> series; it looks attractive, but the experience has been all sorts of terrible, and for some damn reason I am compelled to finish this series despite knowing better. I can't guarantee that it won't damage my eyes, either...it IS over 500 pages. Good god. And that's not to mention the painful experience of actually reading it.<br><br>I can hear some of the complaints now. "Khanh...you fucking idiot, if you hate the series so much, why are you reading it? <b>WHY ARE YOU SUCH A HATER?!</b>" Simple. I am always drawn to siren/mermaid type stories, especially with the <b>lure of combined mythology</b>. This is also an YA series, so it's easier to finish, unlike some of a much grander scale on my To-Be-Read pile *cough*GameofThrones/Outlander/Fever*cough*. Considering how long this book was, though, I can't say the experience of reading it has been particularly easy, much less so given the <b>poor quality of writing, the completely senseless plot, and the utter mess that comprises the book and series overall</b>. And that's not to mention what a mockery the book made of siren mythology and Greek/Romance mythology in general.<br><br>Within this series, some books have been better than others, but that's not saying much. It's like eating maggoty bread, some pieces of bread may have a few less maggots in it, but that's not to say eating it is a more enjoyable experience.<br><br>Enough with the overextended metaphors, I should probably give a few reasons to justify my disdain and hatred for this series. To keep it short (ha!), I will limit it to a top 10.<br><br>In no particular order of perceived pain:<br><br>1. <u>The Roman goddess Diana: also known as Demeter!</u>: Lest we forget who Diana is:<blockquote>"Diana is <b>a Roman goddess of hunting and the moon and werewolves or something</b>. She’s this strong feminist, and certain Wiccans worship her.”</blockquote>ARE YOU FUCKING SERIOUS?<br><br>Btw: Horace = the Egyptian god Horus<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380433254i/871755.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For those who missed the joke: Diana and Demeter are two completely unrelated goddesses...<br><br>2. <u>The sirens</u>: <b>“You little bitch,” Penn said, smiling wider. “Bring it.”</b><br>I referred to them in my last review as <i>The Real Housewives of Orange County</i>. This has not changed. Cattiness, bitchiness, hair-pulling, all still there. I am still amazed at the fact that they've managed to live all these millennium and only managed to kill each other a few times. I would have guessed the murderous turnover ratio within the sirens, at the rate in which they were going in these books, to be at least 100% (death ratio) every 3 weeks or so. I was so sick of the name-calling, the pure hatred between them. It's just common sense...if you're going to be spending a long, long time with someone, be it a friend, a life partner...you find someone you can fucking TRUST. Thea, Penn, &amp; co. just seem to pick and choose who to become the next siren without reason at all. They end up hating each others' guts...I just can't understand it.<br><br>3. <u>Liv</u>: <b>"Penn told you that we wanted you to keep an eye on Harper. But instead of doing that, you attacked her, then went on a spree and killed three people, including a psych teacher."</b><br>Ah, Liv, a.k.a. the worst little siren that ever lived. The sirens aren't exactly the most inconspicuous characters...which is pretty stupid. I mean, if you're trying to <i>survive</i>, it's best to blend in. The original sirens don't exactly do the best job of that, but man, Liv is just something else. She makes the other sirens look like quiet, well-behaved chameleons. She just kills/seduces whomever she feels like it. There's even less subtlety with this one.<br><br>4. <u>Gemma &amp; Harper</u>: Dull as dishwater. I'll give the sirens some credit...they have personality. Gemma and Harper, the two biological sisters, and the two main characters in the book, have no personality, none. I can tell you that Gemma likes swimming, and Alex, she loves her family, and she hates being a siren. But all that you can learn from the first book, because there is nothing, absolutely nothing that you can glean from her character and her mind and her thoughts besides for her single-minded purpose of finding the key to breaking her curse of being a siren, and meanwhile, <b>HOW TO DENY HER CARNAL SIREN URGES *clutches pearls*</b>. Oh, my goodness goshness.<br><br>I stand corrected, Harper does have a personality: that of a middle-aged suburbian housewife in Kansas. But I really shouldn't say that; <b>it's a discourtesy to housewives everywhere to be compared to someone so dull</b>.<br><br>5. <u>Alex</u>: I should rename my doormat to "Alex." Yes, Gemma manipulated you and your mind, she almost made you go permanently Lady-Gaga with her siren song. But oh well, time to forgive at the drop of a hat! Oh, and you should probably apologize to her, anyway, because---um. Because...<br><br>Whatever, just apologize.<br><br>6. <u>Nathalie</u>: I fucking hate it when brain damage = CHILDLIKE BEHAVIOR. <b>It's fucking dumb, it's fucking ignorant, and it is fucking offensive.</b><br><br>7. <u>Daniel</u>: OH NOES I HAVE TO HAVE SEX WITH SOMEONE ELSE FOR THE SAKE OF MY BELOVED GIRLFRIEND. It's all for your own good, baby, really! I'm not even gonna tell you that a manipulate bitch of a siren has her claws into me and is using me because then you'll just make me stop listening to her and put myself at risk. And I really love you, so I have to do this. FOR US! <b>I'm thinking of you as she's straddling me, really</b>.<br><br>8. <u>Professor Kipling Pine</u>: looking past the absolutely Gary Stu name, he's also a young stud. A full professor at an university by his early 30s who looks like a young Indiana Jones. "A history teacher who used to be an archaeologist," who happens to know archaic languages, can identify Aramaic from Phoenician, etc. Man, where was he when I went to college? Most of my professors were in their 40s, at least, and none of them were into steampunk. So sad.<br><br>9. <u>Red Bull</u>: a crucial plot device<br><br>10. <u>Plot &amp; writing</u>: nonsensical, full of holes. The book was also completely plot-driven, leaving no room for character holes, and I ended up being absolutely bored with the entire book, despite all that was taking place. There was no dull moment, but there was plenty of dullness. I read it, but it did not grip me at all. The writing is purely YA, there's nothing beautiful about it, <b>it's easy to read, and that is the best I can say for the writing</b>.<br><br>11. <u>
  <i>Deus ex machi</i>
</u>---oh, wait, I promised to limit it to a list of 10.<br><br>Thank the gods, it's over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1425654297401350486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer15395177921171331139"><b>This review contains spoilers for the first three novels in the <i>Watering</i> series! Read with caution!</b><br/><br/>You know, the length of this book kind of took me by surprise.<br/><br/>542 pages. For Hocking, this is abnormal; her <i>Switched</i> books were all short, clocking in at around 300 pages apiece, and the other <i>Watersong</i> books were each around that length, too. In a 542-page tome, I was worried Hocking would stray from the main mission and divulge too much side information. I was worried the series she has spent thr</span>
  <span id="freeText15395177921171331139" style="display:none"><b>This review contains spoilers for the first three novels in the <i>Watering</i> series! Read with caution!</b><br /><br />You know, the length of this book kind of took me by surprise.<br /><br />542 pages. For Hocking, this is abnormal; her <i>Switched</i> books were all short, clocking in at around 300 pages apiece, and the other <i>Watersong</i> books were each around that length, too. In a 542-page tome, I was worried Hocking would stray from the main mission and divulge too much side information. I was worried the series she has spent three books crafting would crash and burn with an overbearing fourth installment.<br /><br />Those worries were definitely unnecessary.<br /><br />In <i>Elegy</i>, Gemma is closer than ever to breaking the siren curse. With the scroll in her possession, she is almost there. With Penn's impending threats and a ticking clock, she needs to crack the case. The <i>Watersong</i> series ends with the best book, in my opinion. Family drama, sizzling romance, and a touch of the paranormal combine to make <i>Elegy</i> a spellbinding finale to the series. The characters read like your favorite TV family. The strongest offering of Hocking's and my favorite underwater series I've read yet!</span>

<div id="review_582418462" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/582418462" />
    <a title="doctor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13387642-doctor"><img alt="doctor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525376502p2/13387642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/582418462?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="doctor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="doctor" href="/user/show/13387642-doctor">doctor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13387642-doctor?shelf=2k13">2k13</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13387642-doctor?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582418462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7857860543673031631">Well I did it.<br/>I finished the book.<br/>Onto the review, I suppose.<br/>The nice thing about reading books that you either really like or dislike is that you have a lot to say when you're done with them. You aren't left somewhere in the middle (ahem,Unearthly) in which you don't really have a say in things. I went into the Watersong series with high hopes, watched as they got dashed across the pavement in a gorey mess, and then skimmed through the last 50 pages because holy shit, I never did care, and espe</span>
  <span id="freeText7857860543673031631" style="display:none">Well I did it.<br />I finished the book.<br />Onto the review, I suppose.<br />The nice thing about reading books that you either really like or dislike is that you have a lot to say when you're done with them. You aren't left somewhere in the middle (ahem,Unearthly) in which you don't really have a say in things. I went into the Watersong series with high hopes, watched as they got dashed across the pavement in a gorey mess, and then skimmed through the last 50 pages because holy shit, I never did care, and especially now I REALLY don't care.<br />SO anyways, Gemma and company are still under duress trying to turn her back into a normal teenager when in fact they should be focusing on how to destroy Penn and Liv and have a super awesome siren team killing horrible people. (Hell, Thea, Gemma, Harper, and Daniel could do it. In fact I would have liked the story 100x better if that's what had happened.) Penn's new little crony is not worth even complaining about, given how flat and stereotyped her character was.<br />There were so many scenes in which we were assaulted with dialogue of things that did not matter. I think an entire 10 page chapter was dedicated to how Gemma and Alex fell in love. SNORE. BOO. HISS. I don't care. I don't think anybody cares at this point. <br />Penn is a fucking psycho slut. Now, let me just say that I'm totally aware of what "slut shaming" is. Do you know what I think a slut is? Someone who uses sex to hurt people (and not in the wonderful BDSM way). As an advantage. So she's a slut who manipulates and almost RAPES Daniel- which doesn't just hurt him mentally AND PHYSICALLY as we later see, but Harper as well. <br />I'm so glad this is done and over with. Thanks to Walmart for giving this to me for 10.00 instead of 17.99. You're a real bro.<br /></span>

<div id="review_612034871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/612034871" />
    <a title="Paranormal_Madness" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17012067-paranormal-madness"><img alt="Paranormal_Madness" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468451974p2/17012067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/612034871?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paranormal_Madness" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paranormal_Madness" href="/user/show/17012067-paranormal-madness">Paranormal_Madness</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer612034871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8427579169930721871">Warning: This will be very long, there may be spoilers for anyone who hasn't read the other three books, and some of it may be ranty. I have very mixed feelings about this book. Read at your own caution.<br/><br/><b>What I liked:</b><br/>-Thea. She was my favorite part of this book, and probably my favorite part of the series overall. At first, she was just kind of <i>there</i>, not really doing or saying much throughout the story. But she was gradually given a very distinct personality and a tragic back story, and she quic</span>
  <span id="freeText8427579169930721871" style="display:none">Warning: This will be very long, there may be spoilers for anyone who hasn't read the other three books, and some of it may be ranty. I have very mixed feelings about this book. Read at your own caution.<br /><br /><b>What I liked:</b><br />-Thea. She was my favorite part of this book, and probably my favorite part of the series overall. At first, she was just kind of <i>there</i>, not really doing or saying much throughout the story. But she was gradually given a very distinct personality and a tragic back story, and she quickly became my favorite character. I loved the choices she made in the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Her final chapter was very sad for me, since I had grown to like her so much, but in a way, it wasn’t as heartbreaking as I thought. I was left with an odd sense of happiness at the thought of Thea’s suffering being over, and I hoped that she found the peace she was looking for. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />-Gemma. She really, really grew on me in this book. To me, she finally stopped being a whiny, boring, flat character. Instead, she became this badass who wasn’t afraid to us her siren powers to save the people she loved. She fought and clawed her way through this book, refusing to go down without a fight. The fight scenes with Gemma were probably the most exciting part of this book, and honestly, when I first started it, I didn’t think she had it in her to keep fighting. I almost thought she’d just give up.<br /><br /><b>What I disliked:</b><br />-Greek Mythology. One thing I hate more than anything in books is when authors butcher my beloved Greek Mythology, and <i>Elegy</i> did just that. So, we know that the sirens were created by the Greek goddess of the harvest—Demeter—after they fail to protect Demeter’s daughter Persephone, and Persephone is abducted, raped, and murdered. This does not happen in Greek Mythology. Persephone is abducted by Hades, Lord of the Underworld, becomes his bride, and lives with him for eternity. It’s bad enough that her story was twisted, but it gets worse. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, in the story, the group is searching for Diana, who they think is still alive and is going to be able to help them. Diana is the Roman goddess of the hunt and the moon, which makes no sense since the curse is Greek in origin, and I’m pretty sure you can’t actually mix the two. Diana/Artemis are the same goddess, just called by a different name, so why she chose Diana instead I guess I’ll never know? Anyways, they magically track Diana down, and low and behold…Diana is actually Demeter. Hocking took a Roman goddess of the moon and the Greek goddess of the harvest, and smashed them together in one completely stupid and poorly researched goddess that doesn’t exist in any mythology book. Okay then. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The whole Greek Mythology element was the main reason I enjoyed this series, since it has always been a huge love of mine, and it ended being the worst part of the book for me. It brought nothing new to the story and it actually made me so angry I considered not finishing it. If you’re a mythology fanatic like me, stay away.<br />-Daniel. I really loved his character throughout the first three books, but honestly, it felt like he lost some of his magic and charm in this one. He wasn’t the same character I loved before, and since he was one of my favorites, that really made this book less enjoyable than I thought it would be.<br />-Penn and Liv. For being the two major antagonists of this book and the series, they were awfully catty and bitchy. There wasn’t a whole lot of substance to them, even though Penn gradually got a bit of back story and personality. For the most part, Penn was just the “top bitch” that flaunted her body and power every chance she got. And Liv was just a violent psychopath that I didn’t ever really take seriously. She was just crazy, and not in a fleshed out, detailed, believable way.<br />-Length and pace. This book—at 542 pages—was a beast. It took me way too long to finish, because I just didn’t really get into it all that much. I went days at a time without even picking it up, and I didn’t have the motivation to read. I honestly didn’t rally care about what happened to most of the characters. I was never really drawn into this book, and it was kind of boring. There were unbearably long chunks where nothing happens, and I felt like a lot of it could have been edited out.<br />-POV. There were so many freaking point of views in this book I couldn’t take it. I hate it when there are two or more point of views, but this one had like six! Gemma, Harper, Daniel, Marcy, Alex, and Thea—I think I got them all. It felt like a lot of these little four or five page long chapters were just added in there to draw the story out and make it longer. Towards the end, while the huge climax was taking place, it kept switching to some boring point of view that didn’t matter, and that was awful. The point the entire series had been building up to kept getting interrupted, and at that point, I just didn’t care.<br />-The ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One thing I hate in books is that perfect fairy-tale ending where everything just works out and is all magical and perfect. Seriously, every freaking person in this story got a perfect ending. Everybody ended up with someone. Even Gemma and Harper’s dad started dating someone! And Mary was “dating” Kirby’s ghost! What? And Daniel proposing to Harper was just the icing on the already overly sweet cake, and I hated it. She’s eighteen, maybe nineteen, and they’ve been dating for at most a year? Everything in her character up until that point pointed to her refusing to get married anytime soon, but she just says yes? Fairy-tale endings are terrible, and Hocking has a problem with doing it all the time. She needs to tone it down a little. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, this was by far the worst book in the series. I was so disappointed when I reached the last page, and was left thinking, “That’s it? Four books…and that’s all I get?” I loved many of the characters, but the pace was all off and there was so much unnecessary filler, and then there's the butchered Greek Mythology. If you’re a hardcore fan of Amanda Hocking or the Watersong series, you’ll probably love it, but I wouldn’t recommend it for anyone else, unless you really love sirens—like crazy love them. I’m just glad it’s over. <b>2.0</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8427579169930721871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14031162272849427990">I got sucked into this book and couldn't stop reading it. I HAD to know what was going to happen next! The last 80 pages or so flew by, I couldn't get to the ending fast enough. This has become one of my favorite series now. I love reading books about strong female characters. The last 80 pages or so flew by, I couldn't get to the ending fast enough. This has become one of my favorite series now. I love reading books about strong female characters. As a girl it is definitely awesome to see that. I just wish I had more of it when I was growing up, but we have it now so that's wonderful!<br /><br />I wasn't sure about these books when I first got them. I didn't think I would enjoy the mermaid/siren thing, but I actually really loved it. I got a little mad at Thea in this one. She annoyed me. She was older than Penn and she let Penn push her around for too long. I thought she would finally put Penn in her place, but she never did. I really did not like Liv. I enjoyed Lexi far more than I did Liv. She was too whiny and annoying. I wanted to rip her head off before she became a siren lol.<br /><br />Anyway, if you enjoyed Trylle then you should definitely give this one a try! I am glad that I did!</span>

<div id="review_2434409318" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2434409318" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2434409318?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=paranormal-urban-fantasy">paranormal-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=meh-reads">meh-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2434409318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9139130769032137681">There were times where I felt like this was the most ridiculous book I've read in a long time. I don't know how but the series only got worse with each book. This one was also way way too long. The first two books were the right length for this kind of easy read (300 pages or under it), the tird book was a bit over it, but this one was over 500 pages of stretched out plot and DRAMA. I enjoyed (a little) reading the first two, but the next two in the series were a disaster to me. Especially this </span>
  <span id="freeText9139130769032137681" style="display:none">There were times where I felt like this was the most ridiculous book I've read in a long time. I don't know how but the series only got worse with each book. This one was also way way too long. The first two books were the right length for this kind of easy read (300 pages or under it), the tird book was a bit over it, but this one was over 500 pages of stretched out plot and DRAMA. I enjoyed (a little) reading the first two, but the next two in the series were a disaster to me. Especially this one. Sometimes it seemed like a parody of a book even. There were some super serious and (supposedly) 'emotional' moments that made me laugh so hard at how ridiculous it all was. The whole Penn x Daniel thing was fucking ridiculous too <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[“Oh my god, Daniel.” Harper gasped. “What is she doing to you?” ... LMAO I can't even. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I couldn't take it seriously at all. The sirens were either bitchy or downright stupid. Gemma was uninteresting. Harper somewhat likeable. Daniel I still hated ever since book three. And Alex was just a doormat when it came to Gemma. Riddikulus, I say!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9139130769032137681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1117864561715794998">I have three main issues with the final book in the Watersong series. 1: Don't tell me Daniel's birthday is a week before Labor Day and then tell me he's a Scorpio. Continuity! 2: I felt like the author brought in a bunch of new characters in this book and all of them served little to no purpose. Like she tried really hard to keep the reader guessing but it just wasn't working for me. 3: The fact that everyone got such perfect happy endings kinda makes me wanna vom. I'd call it Breaking Dawn syn</span>
  <span id="freeText1117864561715794998" style="display:none">I have three main issues with the final book in the Watersong series. 1: Don't tell me Daniel's birthday is a week before Labor Day and then tell me he's a Scorpio. Continuity! 2: I felt like the author brought in a bunch of new characters in this book and all of them served little to no purpose. Like she tried really hard to keep the reader guessing but it just wasn't working for me. 3: The fact that everyone got such perfect happy endings kinda makes me wanna vom. I'd call it Breaking Dawn syndrome. It's like all of this crazy life-threatening traumatic stuff happened and then everyone said "Gee, what a crazy summer, huh?" and went on with their lives.</span>

<div id="review_696603053" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696603053" />
    <a title="Roxanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15602675-roxanne"><img alt="Roxanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581473386p2/15602675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696603053?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxanne" href="/user/show/15602675-roxanne">Roxanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15602675-roxanne?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15602675-roxanne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15602675-roxanne?shelf=mermaids-sirens">mermaids-sirens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696603053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7901318597276889855">When I saw this in the store, I was like "how the hell did the series go from being 300 pages each book to nearly 600 hundred?" And I gotta say, bigger is not better.<br/><br/>First off, I'm going to put this out there right now. This is one of those book series where the characters lose absolutely NOTHING in the end <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I guess maybe Kirby was a loss...but no one seemed to give a shit except Marcy but that's not saying much <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The characters get everything they want and more. <br/><br/>On </span>
  <span id="freeText7901318597276889855" style="display:none">When I saw this in the store, I was like "how the hell did the series go from being 300 pages each book to nearly 600 hundred?" And I gotta say, bigger is not better.<br /><br />First off, I'm going to put this out there right now. This is one of those book series where the characters lose absolutely NOTHING in the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I guess maybe Kirby was a loss...but no one seemed to give a shit except Marcy but that's not saying much <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The characters get everything they want and more. <br /><br />On top of that, the characters haven't changed since book one. Gemma and Harper are still dull as freaking rocks; Alex is as interesting as a rug; Daniel is the ever perfect boyfriend that waits for his girlfriend to put out; and Penn is still a bitch. NONE OF THIS HAS CHANGED.<br /><br />And I swear to Christ, if Gemma says how she doesn't want to be a monster and kill people one more time, I'll burn the book. Penn describes Gemma as "unbreakable"...I describe her as being a wussy little bitch that, clearly, is not willing to do anything to stay alive.<br /><br />Every single problem in this series is solved in this final installment. I feel like I've just been reading the same book over and over again because the same problems are repeated every chapter. You know, just in case you missed it the first 50 times it was repeated in the chapter before. <br /><br />Also, this book seemed to me to just be a longer version of Tidal. It's boring as hell. There is some action here and there, but overall I was bored with it and couldn't wait to be finished with it.<br /><br />The last thing that really, really pissed me off while reading it was Amanda Hocking taking a shit all over Greek Mythology. DEMETER AND DIANA ARE COMPLETELY TWO DIFFERENT, UNRELATED GODDESSES GODDAMNIT!!!!!!!! <br /><br />The series started out fun for me, really. I thought it was a fun series, but I have my limits. There's only so much stupidity I can take. I'm glad the series is over.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7901318597276889855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_637827204" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637827204" />
    <a title="LB" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18156604-lb"><img alt="LB" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370519085p2/18156604.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/637827204?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LB" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LB" href="/user/show/18156604-lb">LB</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18156604-lb?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18156604-lb?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18156604-lb?shelf=under-the-sea">under-the-sea</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637827204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16437773343728163069">This review is also posted at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://readingnookandcranny.blogspot.com/2013/08/elegy.html'>http://readingnookandcranny.blogspot....</a><br/><br/>Well, I can honestly say this book (let's be honest, the entire series in general) did not live up to my expectations. I now feel I need to go back and reread the Trylle trilogy to see if it was actually any good after finishing this series.<br/><br/>Let's start with the characters. They are cliche and one dimensional. For a while, in perhaps the first or second book, there were a few of them that I actually liked. In the middle of the </span>
  <span id="freeText16437773343728163069" style="display:none">This review is also posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readingnookandcranny.blogspot.com/2013/08/elegy.html">http://readingnookandcranny.blogspot....</a><br /><br />Well, I can honestly say this book (let's be honest, the entire series in general) did not live up to my expectations. I now feel I need to go back and reread the Trylle trilogy to see if it was actually any good after finishing this series.<br /><br />Let's start with the characters. They are cliche and one dimensional. For a while, in perhaps the first or second book, there were a few of them that I actually liked. In the middle of the series, I found myself favoring different characters than in the beginning. But by the end, I hated them all. Most of them were whiny and bitching. The ones that weren't were annoying in their own ways.<br /><br />Then we get to the plot. Sure, the whole siren thing is resolved, but it is pretty typical. Not a surprise in store there at all. And while this book is about 530 pages long, not much of it is actual, honest plot. Most of it is typical YA romance junk. With a group of teenagers and young 20s characters, especially a bunch of extraordinarily beautiful girls, I expected some of this. I even tolerated it for the first two books in the series. The third one got a little annoying, especially with the Penn/Daniel subplot. But, by goly, but the time we get to Elegy, it seems as if raging hormones are running amok. Everyone is making out and a lot of them are having sex (and it appears as if it is unprotected sex as well - not exactly a message I would want to be sending out to young girls, certainly not if I were raising a daughter). While I rolled my eyes at it in the third book, in Elegy it all just wanted to make be barf.<br /><br />I definitely won't be adding the boxed set of this series to my collection. I will not even be borrowing it from the library to read again. I am going to tuck it safely away in a recess in the corner of my mind and pretend like I never read them. Hocking lost quite a bit of respect/admiration from me for this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16437773343728163069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer8419804783112547446">This is the most fun series and I am so sad that it's over. On the plus side, the last book was a complete brick (almost 550 pages) and that gave me plenty of time to say goodbye to Gemma, Alex, Harper, Daniel and everyone else. (Yes, even Penn.)<br/><br/>I loved the mythology of this book and hope that we can visit a different story in this world. (In this land of gods and goddesses and presumed-to-be mythical creatures, you can't tell me that there's not spinoff potential.)<br/><br/>The pacing in this last book i</span>
  <span id="freeText8419804783112547446" style="display:none">This is the most fun series and I am so sad that it's over. On the plus side, the last book was a complete brick (almost 550 pages) and that gave me plenty of time to say goodbye to Gemma, Alex, Harper, Daniel and everyone else. (Yes, even Penn.)<br /><br />I loved the mythology of this book and hope that we can visit a different story in this world. (In this land of gods and goddesses and presumed-to-be mythical creatures, you can't tell me that there's not spinoff potential.)<br /><br />The pacing in this last book is perfect. We get answers but of course those only tend to lead to more questions. Even so, it serves to keep the reader engaged without leading to frustration and/or boredom. (I think we all know the books that lead to the reader losing all interest because the author just keeps piling on question after question without providing answers.)<br /><br />I enjoyed her Trylle series but the Watersong books show how much she's grown as an author. This series is just fantastic and I can't think of any way to improve it.<br /><br />Highly recommended. (Especially now, when you can read all the books in a row.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8419804783112547446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5362178740134739187">*SPOILER ALERT* Meh. I expected more from this book. A lot more. First of all it could have been 200 pages less. I found it dragged and was really annoyed by most of it rehashing the same siren threats and character angsts over (and over and over) again. Also, Amanda Hocking should NOT write sex scenes. Just...No. The wording was SOOO awkward, it reminded me of one of the cheap harlequin novels. If you're not comfortable writing it, readers can tell. Should have just stuck to make out scenes. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText5362178740134739187" style="display:none">*SPOILER ALERT* Meh. I expected more from this book. A lot more. First of all it could have been 200 pages less. I found it dragged and was really annoyed by most of it rehashing the same siren threats and character angsts over (and over and over) again. Also, Amanda Hocking should NOT write sex scenes. Just...No. The wording was SOOO awkward, it reminded me of one of the cheap harlequin novels. If you're not comfortable writing it, readers can tell. Should have just stuck to make out scenes. The ending and "solution" to breaking the siren curse was incredibly transparent and obvious. I wanted to hit the characters over the head they were so clueless about it. Really a disappointing ending to what had been a good interesting series. </span>

<div id="review_1522874903" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1522874903" />
    <a title="☆Stephanie☆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20199767-stephanie"><img alt="☆Stephanie☆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521760196p2/20199767.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522874903?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☆Stephanie☆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☆Stephanie☆" href="/user/show/20199767-stephanie">☆Stephanie☆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20199767-stephanie?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20199767-stephanie?shelf=ya-mythology">ya-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522874903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9549419707919285563">As I've said before, I'm a big fan of the <i>Watersong</i> series. It took me a long time to finish because I started reading from NetGalley, and picked up a TON of books from the library, and this final chapter of the quartet was put on the back burner. Then I realized it was due tomorrow.<br/>Well, for my birthday present today, I stayed in and finished all 542 pages of the book. I loved the ending to series as a whole. It all comes full-circle, and it ends just perfectly. Despite Hocking still using the </span>
  <span id="freeText9549419707919285563" style="display:none">As I've said before, I'm a big fan of the <i>Watersong</i> series. It took me a long time to finish because I started reading from NetGalley, and picked up a TON of books from the library, and this final chapter of the quartet was put on the back burner. Then I realized it was due tomorrow.<br />Well, for my birthday present today, I stayed in and finished all 542 pages of the book. I loved the ending to series as a whole. It all comes full-circle, and it ends just perfectly. Despite Hocking still using the word "foxy" once or twice (I still hate that word for "sexy"... No one uses it!), <i>Elegy</i> left nothing to be desired.<br />Gemma and Harper have fought the siren curse for three books, and during the fourth they've both found love, and friendship, and know that they must finally take down Penn before she destroys all their lives. Talk about a sociopathic bitch: I don't think I've hated a character more. But I enjoy the close relationship between the sisters and their desperate desire to save Gemma, and rid her of siren bitches forever. I'm not going to spoil the series for anyone (but if you're reading this book, you've read the other three, obviously, so you know what's going on), but I will say that all books lead up to this one: the 542 pages fly by as you scramble along with the main characters, trying to break the scroll's unbreakable curse. And we finally meet Demeter, and she's justifiably pissed, still after thousands of years. Talk about holding a grudge! (I mean, the sirens didn't kill Persephone; they were just distracted when it happened...talk about not having closure!).<br />Anyway, if you're a fan of mythology, Sirens, or mermaids, these books are for you. Start with the first novel, <i>Wake</i>, and get lost in Hocking's comfortably casual prose. She writes like you're a best friend, and she leaves nothing out...she trusts you with the characters' feelings and thoughts, and you feel Harper's frustration and Gemma's anger. I'm tempted to try the <i>Trylle</i> series after this one...I'm a fan now.<br />And I dig the Siren myths...mermaids and Sirens are really fascinating, beautifully evil, and/or tragically cursed. Love it. Makes my life feel way less complicated. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9549419707919285563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_328282028" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/328282028" />
    <a title="Brad Sells" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3365948-brad-sells"><img alt="Brad Sells" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578588259p2/3365948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/328282028?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad Sells" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad Sells" href="/user/show/3365948-brad-sells">Brad Sells</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365948-brad-sells?shelf=arc-own">arc-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365948-brad-sells?shelf=finished-copy-for-review">finished-copy-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365948-brad-sells?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365948-brad-sells?shelf=2013-top-13">2013-top-13</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365948-brad-sells?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer328282028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10644292735813331640"><b> This review is entirely spoiler free, even if you haven't started this series. </b><br/><br/>Elegy is a fantastic and phenomenal conclusion to one of the best series I have ever read. Amanda Hocking's vivid world is riveting, chilling, and simply stunning - I couldn't have asked for a better ending!<br/><br/>Amanda Hocking is one of my favorite authors of all-time, and I can officially say that the Watersong Quartet is one of my favorite series ever. They're so addicting and amazing! And in Elegy, more risks are takin</span>
  <span id="freeText10644292735813331640" style="display:none"><b> This review is entirely spoiler free, even if you haven't started this series. </b><br /><br />Elegy is a fantastic and phenomenal conclusion to one of the best series I have ever read. Amanda Hocking's vivid world is riveting, chilling, and simply stunning - I couldn't have asked for a better ending!<br /><br />Amanda Hocking is one of my favorite authors of all-time, and I can officially say that the Watersong Quartet is one of my favorite series ever. They're so addicting and amazing! And in Elegy, more risks are taking and the action scenes are insane. Right from the first page, we're thrown into a tension-filled, nail-biting scene, and it never, ever stops. And I want to applaud Amanda Hocking for creating this brilliant series - she definitely pushed her characters to the max and challenged them in ways I couldn't even fathom. I loved how she broke them and destroyed them, which only makes them stronger. All of the characters shine out in Elegy, and it's fantastically incredible.<br /><br />Another thing I love about this series is how it doesn't focus on one or two particular characters. In book one, Wake, we mainly see Gemma and Harper. But as the series progresses, we get inside Daniel's, Penn's, Sawyer's, and even more characters's heads. It can be very hard to juggle so many POVs, but Hocking tackles it masterfully. I was never once confused, and this series is the perfect balance of paranormal and romance. The Watersong Quartet is one of the best series out there, and I highly, highly recommend it!<br /><br />That. Ending. I'm still not over. I had no idea how Hocking would end the series. There were many ways that Elegy could have concluded, but the path that was chosen was not only satisfying, but rich and deep - it worked perfect for the series. And since this is a complex series, I was definitely satisfied and fell in love with this finale. Hocking fans, rejoice! You are going to love Elegy - one of the best conclusions to a series ever.<br /><br />Overall, Elegy was fantastic, phenomenal, and entirely marvelous. I'm so sad to let this series go, but it ended so great. Thank you, Amanda Hocking, for this journey - I loved every single moment of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10644292735813331640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9455936873347693583">So i liked this book and i really liked how it ended. I have been reading a couple books with bad endings so this helped with that. As with the other books in this series, there were problems.<br/><br/>Lets start with the good parts of this book. I liked the ending. There were no loose ends. Everything was closed and you aren't left asking any questions. Everyone gets their little happy every after and all is well in the world. Nothing annoys me more than open endings. <br/><br/>Now come the not so good parts. As w</span>
  <span id="freeText9455936873347693583" style="display:none">So i liked this book and i really liked how it ended. I have been reading a couple books with bad endings so this helped with that. As with the other books in this series, there were problems.<br /><br />Lets start with the good parts of this book. I liked the ending. There were no loose ends. Everything was closed and you aren't left asking any questions. Everyone gets their little happy every after and all is well in the world. Nothing annoys me more than open endings. <br /><br />Now come the not so good parts. As with the other books in this series, the characters were dull, duller and dullest. I feel like its the 3rd persond pov thats stoping me from connceting with these characters because I just didn't like em. The sirens were evil but at least they had personality. I liked Daniel and Harper in the first two books with their cute banter but once they got together, it was boring! Gemma and Alex were boring too. I know nothing about Gemma besides the fact that she doesnt want to be a siren. As for Haprer, she has a bit personality but hers is annoying. <br /> Another problem with this book was that there were very unrealistic things happening. I don't want to spoil so I won't say but if you've read the book then you know were I'm comming from. <br /><br />So overall, I liked this book and series. Not one of my favorites, like Amanda's other series, bit it was ok. <br /><br /><br /><br />*******SPOILERS!!!!!******<br /><br />Now lets talk about the big fight scene at the siren's house. Can someone explain to me how Haprer can be thrown from a second floor balcony and onto a wooden coffee table and then get up and search for a weapon to help Gemma without any difficulty? I was baffled. <br /> 500 pages of this book were devoted to breaking the curse and she breaks it in the last ten pages. And how did she not think to go in the water, use the shawl and the blood like the night she turned into a siren?! I thought about that when Gemma tried with her blood at home and it takes her 500+ pages to figure it out. And she wasn't even trying! The whole "figure it out" part of the last 10 pages was an accident.<br /> So yeah.... Those are my thoughts on this book</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7818077173377584831">I am not that good at reviews.. but here it goes.<br/>I was very dissapointed in these books, after reading Hockings Tyrlle series I thought this would be just as good.. but they were not as good.   <span id="freeText7818077173377584831" style="display:none">I am not that good at reviews.. but here it goes.<br />I was very dissapointed in these books, after reading Hockings Tyrlle series I thought this would be just as good.. but they were not as good. The sirens themselves were very captivating and kept me reading because I wanted to see how the curse would or wouldn't be broken. If it wasn't for that I probably wouldnt have finished all of the books. <br />In his particular book, Gemma, Harper, Marcy, along with some other friends are trying to figure out how to break the curse of the sirens with the scroll given to them by Thea.. which I thought was a little to easy. All he while, a new siren is born and causes so much trouble, but yet Penn goes out of character to not care even though she is the one in charge and hasn't ever let anyone do as they please without her permission. When they do find the answer to whether or not they can break the curse I found that to be a little to easy also,.... spolier! ... why would Demeter tell them she would never tell them how to break the curse yet do it anyways? I didn't make sense to me. I also felt like throughout the entire series Hocking just used too much filler, twlling us things that had happened before even though you already knew that it happened... honestly, it wouldn't have been that long of a series if she hadn't done that and it wouldn't have been so frustrating to read. I found myself sayng.. "I know that already!" alot throughtout the series.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vBXhnWIv6s2TDUp2cjvn35sKizmd8Xjm8YlgXz+00RkymTpiJhp7imR93v58Vzl+6UC/rDVGW0Tt3S22U9YAnA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('R68vgA10Bi2B1+n9/8GKpd/VqiZOv6YuUFKmK/Fxr/fJI/R/SUGXananfXXxrVQErZ+es+YIhYxMBuvCnRN+cg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer8268914928516433311">AMANDA HOCKING is the author of over twenty young adult novels, including the New York Times bestselling Trylle Trilogy and Kanin Chronicles. Her zombie series</span>
  <span id="freeText8268914928516433311" style="display:none">AMANDA HOCKING is the author of over twenty young adult novels, including the New York Times bestselling Trylle Trilogy and Kanin Chronicles. Her love of pop culture and all things paranormal influence her writing. She spends her time in Minnesota, taking care of her menagerie of pets and working on her next book.<br /><br />Several of her books have made the New York Times Bestsellers list. Her zombie series, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/hollowland-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hollows</a>, has been adapted into a graphic novel by Dynamite. She has published over twenty novels, including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/48928-trylle&gt; the Trylle Trilogy&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kanin Chronicles</a>, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/watersong-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">the Watersong quartet</a>, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/my-blood-approves-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blood Approves series</a>, the Valkyrie duology<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/150484-valkyrie" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25184362-freeks#other_reviews" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Freeks</em>
</a>.<br /><br />Her next books are the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47590299-the-lost-city" rel="nofollow noopener"> Omte Origins</a>, a trilogy set in the world of the Trylle and Kanin. The first book <em> The Lost City</em> will be out July 7, 2020, and the second book <em> The Morning Flower </em> will be out August 5, 2020. <br /><br />For more info about her and her books, here are some other places to check out and ways to contact her:<br /><br />Website: <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">www.hockingbooks.com</a><br /><br />Amazon Author Page: <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Amanda-Hocking/e/B003H4L762" rel="nofollow noopener">amazon.com/author/amandahocking</a><br /><br />Instagram: <a href="https://instagram.com/amanda_hocking/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram.com/amanda_hocking/</a><br /><br />YouTube: <a href="https://www.youtube.com/aehocking" rel="nofollow noopener">www.youtube.com/aehocking</a><br /><br /><br />Pinterest: <a href="http://www.pinterest.com/aehocking/" rel="nofollow noopener">www.pinterest.com/aehocking/</a><br /></span>
